Ruling on Imprisoning a Debtor
Explains when and how a debtor is imprisoned

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the specific debts for which a debtor may be imprisoned in the Hanafi school and explain the judge's procedure, including proof of wealth and determination of imprisonment duration.

Core Idea
Imprisonment for debt in Hanafi law is limited to four types of contractual debts; duration is at the judge's discretion.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq explains the Hanafi rules on imprisoning a debtor. It details which debts trigger imprisonment, the conditions required before a judge may imprison, and the ongoing debate over whether the duration of imprisonment should be fixed or discretionary. By studying this passage, you will not only know the ruling but also understand the underlying proofs and the practical application in the judiciary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? Imprisonment of a debtor. What is the hukm? It is a discretionary punishment (ta'zir) to compel payment, obligatory (wajib) on the judge when conditions are met.
The act itself is a judicial measure, not a fixed penalty.
2
Locate the dalil
What proofs are cited? The Quran (5:33 interpreted as imprisonment), Sunnah (the Prophet detained a man on suspicion), and Ijma' (consensus of the Companions).
The Quranic verse originally addresses highway robbers, but the interpretation extends to imprisonment.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does each proof support imprisonment? The phrase 'yufaw min al-ard' is interpreted as confinement; the Sunnah provides a precedent; Ijma' confirms legality.
The Hanafi school uses this as a basis for ta'zir.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
What is the dispute? Over the duration of imprisonment. Some narrations attribute fixed durations (1, 4, or 6 months) to Abu Hanifa, and Malikis have specific limits. The relied-upon view is that duration is at the judge's discretion.
The text states these reports are 'ittifaqi' not definitive.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Which position is relied upon? The correct view (al-sahih) is that duration is delegated to the judge's discretion, as conditions vary by person, time, and circumstance.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب القضاء
فصل في بيان الحبس
وإذا ثبت الحق للمدعي أمره بدفع ما عليه، فإن أبى حبسه في الثمن والقرض والمهر المعجل، وما التزمه بالكفالة لا في غيره إن ادّعى الفقر إلا أن يثبت غريمه غناه، فيحبسه بما رأى ثم يسأل عنه، فإن لم يظهر له مال، خلاه، وهو المدعى عليه
= فكان من
المدعى عليه
ولا يحبسه على الفور
منه
باب التعاون على البر كإرسال الرجل لإحضار الخصم وتكفيله، وحيلولته بينه وبين أشغاله، وأما في موضع التهمة كإن ادعى المدعي ألفاً وخمس مائة والمدعى عليه ينكر خمس مائة، وشهد الشاهدان بالألف، فالقاضي إن قال يحتمل أنه أبرأه من خمس مائة واستفاد الشاهد علما بذلك، ووفق في شهادته كما وفق القاضي فهذا لا يجوز بالاتفاق. (فتح، وجامع الرموز) فصل: أي في بيان الحبس ولما كان بعض الناس يستحق العقوبة بسبب تمرده، والحبس يصلح للعقوبة، ذكره في كتاب القضاء، وجعله من جملته وهو مشروع بالكتاب والسنة والإجماع، أما الكتاب: فقوله تعالى في قطاع الطريق: أَوْ يُنْفَوْا مِنَ الْأَرْضِ الله (المائدة:۳۳) والمراد به الحبس، وأما السنة: فلأنه عليها رجلاً بالتهمة، وأما حبس الإجماع: فلأن الصحابة له ومن بعدهم أجمعوا عليه، ولم يكن في زمنه عليه السلام وأبي بكر وعمر وعثمان الله سجن، وكان يحبس في المجلس أو في المسجد، ولما كان في زمن علي الله بنى السجن، وهو أول من بناه في الإسلام. تبيين الحقائق: ۹۰/۵، ۹۱] وصفة الحبس: أن يكون في موضع خشن ليس فيه فراش ولا وطاء، ولو جيء له بذلك لا يمكن كما لا يمكن أحد يدخل عليه للاستيناس إلا أقاربه أو جيرانه ولكن لا يمكثون، ولا يخرج الجمعة ولا جماعة ولا لحج فرض ولا لحضور جنازة، ولو بكفيل، وكذا لا يخرج بمجيء رمضان والعيدين، وإن مرض مرضاً أضناه فإن وجد من : لا يخرج، وإلا أخرج بكفيل، ولا يخرج لمعالجة وكسب، ولو له دين أ أخرج ليخاصم، ثم يحبس، ولا يغل، ولا يجرد، ولا يؤاجر، ولا يقام بين يدي صاحب الحق إهانة، ولا يضرب ويجعل للنساء سجن على حدة؛ نفيا للفتنة. (فتح) الحق ولو دانقا وهو سدس درهم. (فتح) أمره إلخ: ينبغي أن يقيد بما إذا لم يتمكن القاضي من الدفع إليه بنفسه كما إذا ادعى عيناً في يد غيره، أو وديعة له عنده، وبرهن أنها هي التي في يده، أو ديناً له عليه وبرهن على ذلك، فوجد معه ما هو من جنس حقه، كان للقاضي أ أن يأخذ العين منه، وما هو من جنس حقه، ويدفعه إلى المالك غير محتاج إلى أمره بدفع ما عليه. (فتح) فإن أبى: أي امتنع عن دفع ما عليه إلى المدعي. (عيني) حبسه في الثمن [ أي في كل دين لزمه بدلا عن مال حصل في يده مثل الثمن. (ط، عيني) ] إن الشيخ لم يفصل بين ثبوت الحق ببينة أو بإقرار، وفصل بينهما في "الهداية" فقال: إذا ثبت بالبينة يحبسه ؛ لظهور المطل بإنكاره، وإن ثبت بإقراره لم يعجل بحبسه؛ لأنه لم يعرف كونه مماطلاً في أول الوهلة، فلعله طمع في الإمهال، فلم يستصحب المال، فإذا امتنع بعد ذلك حبسه؛ لظهور مطله، والصواب: أن لا يحبسه فيهما إذا طلب المدعي ذلك، حتى يسأله، فإن أقر أن له مالاً أمره بالدفع، فإن أبي حبسه؛ =

والمهر المعجل، وما التزمه ،بالكفالة لا في غيره إن ادّعى الفقر إلا أن يثبت غريمه
أي وفيما التزمه إلخ
المدعى عليه
غناه، فيحبسه بما رأى ثم يسأل عنه، فإن لم يظهر له مال، خلاه،
القاضي )
الناس أي عن حال المحبوس
أي للمدعى عليه
وهو المدعى
الظهور مطله، وإن أنكر المال، وأقام المدعي البينة أن له مالاً، أمره بالدفع، فإن أبى حبسه، وإن عجز عن البينة ويدعي أن له مالاً، وهو ينكر، كان القول قول المدعى عليه. [رمز الحقائق: ١٢٠/٢] والمهر: أي وفي كل مال التزمه مثل المهر إلخ. (عيني) وما التزمه بالكفالة [ أي وفي كل دين لزمه بعقد؛ لأنه بالإباء ظهر مطله . (عيني)] يعم الكفيل وكفيل الكفيل، وإن كثروا، ويعم الكفالة بالدرك، وفي كل عين يقدر على تسليمها ليشمل حبسه على العين المغصوبة والأمانات إذا امتنع الأمين من دفعها غير مدع هلاكها؛ لأنها صارت مغصوبة. (فتح) لا في غيره أي لا يحبسه في غير ذلك من الديون كضمان الغصب والمتلفات [وأرش الجنايات] وبدل عتق نصيب الشريك وديون النفقات للزوجة أو القريب، وإنما لا يحبس في هذه الأشياء إذا ادعى الفقر؛ لأنه لا دليل على اليسار؛ لأن دليل اليسار إذا لم يوجد كان القول لمن عليه الدين وعلى المدعي إثبات غناه أي قدرته على وفاء الدين، بخلاف الفصل الأول؛ لأنه حيث حصل المال في يده ثبت غناه ،به، وإقدامه على التزامه باختياره دليل يساره. (فتح) الفقر لأنه متمسك بالأصل وهو الفقر عند الأمر بالدفع. (عيني) غناه بدليل شرعي بأن له مالاً ( ط ) عيني) فيحبسه بما رأى [ أي فحينئذ يحبسه لظهور المطل. (عيني)] الباء للتعدية وهي ومدخولها متعلقة بمحذوف حال من الضمير المستتر في "فيحبسه"، و"ما" عبارة عن . مدة وعائدها محذوف والتقدير: فيحبسه مقدرا بمدة رآها من المصلحة حتى يغلب على ظن القاضي أنه لو كان له مال لأظهره، ولم يصبر على مقاساة الحبس، وذلك يختلف باختلاف الشخص والزمان والمكان والمال، فلا معنى لتقديره وما روي عن أبي حنيفة أنه مقدر بشهر وعنه بستة أشهر، وعنه بأربعة أشهر فاتفاقي وليس بتقدير حتماً، والصحيح أن التقدير مفوض إلى رأي القاضي ولو يوماً، وعند بعض المالكية: في القليل لا يجب أكثر من نصف شهر، وفي الكثير أربعة أشهر فقط [ رمز الحقائق: ۱۲۱/۲]
:
ثم يسأل عنه: أي يسأل القاضي عن المحبوس من جيرانه احتياطاً لا وجوباً بعد ما حبسه قدر ما رآه، فإن قامت بينة على إعساره خلاه أي أخرجه من الحبس، ولا يحتاج فيه إلى لفظ الشهادة والعدل الواحد يكفي بغيبة دائن، والاثنان أحوط ولا يشترط حضرة الخصم وكيفيته أن يقول الشاهد: إن حاله حال المعسرين في نفقته وكسوته، وحاله ضيقة، وقد اختبرنا حاله في السر والعلانية رمز الحقائق: ١٢١/٢] (فتح) فإن لم يظهر له إلخ : أي أطلقه من الحبس جبراً على الدائن بلا أخذ كفيل إلا في ثلاث: مال يتيم ووقف وإذا كان الدائن غائبا؛ لأن عسرته ثبت عند القاضي واستحق النظرة إلى الميسرة؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِنْ كَانَ ذُو عُسْرَةٍ فَنَظِرَةٌ إِلَى مَيْسَرَةٍ (البقرة: ۲۸۰) فحبسه بعده يكون ظلما. (عيني، فتح)
خلاه: أي أخرجه من السجن بعد مضي المدة التي رآها في الحبس. (ط، عيني)
Book of Judiciary. Section on Imprisonment. When the claimant's right is established, the judge orders the defendant to pay what is due. If he refuses, he imprisons him for the price, loan, prompt dower, and what he has undertaken by guarantee, but not for other matters if he claims poverty, unless his creditor proves his wealth. Then he imprisons him for a period he deems fit, then inquires about him, and if no wealth appears, he releases him. He does not imprison him immediately. ... The description of imprisonment: it should be in a rough place with no bedding or cushion... and a separate prison is made for women to avoid temptation. ... The correct view is that the duration is delegated to the judge's discretion. ... Then he inquires about the prisoner from his neighbors as a precaution, not an obligation. If evidence of his insolvency appears, he releases him. ... If no wealth appears, he releases him from prison forcibly from the creditor without taking a surety except in three cases: the property of an orphan, a waqf, and when the creditor is absent.
Source pages p. 411

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on the imprisonment of a debtor in Hanafi law. It opens by establishing that when a debt is proven, the judge orders the debtor to pay. If he refuses, the judge can imprison him, but only for specific types of debts: the sale price (thaman), loans (qard), prompt dower (mahr mu'ajjal), and debts undertaken by guarantee (kafala). For other debts like damages for usurpation (daman al-ghasb) or maintenance (nafaqa), if the debtor claims poverty, he is not imprisoned unless the creditor proves his wealth. The judge does not imprison immediately; he first asks the debtor. If the debtor admits to having wealth but refuses, he is imprisoned. If he denies having wealth and the creditor has no proof, the debtor's word is accepted. The imprisonment itself is harsh: a rough place with no comfort, no leaving for Friday or congregational prayers, and no visitors except close relatives briefly. A separate prison is prescribed for women. The duration of imprisonment is at the judge's discretion, not fixed; reports that Abu Hanifa fixed it at a month or six months are not definitive. After the period, the judge inquires about the debtor's condition. If evidence of insolvency appears, the debtor is released, and the creditor must wait for ease as per Quran 2:280. Release is without a surety except for the property of an orphan, waqf, or absent creditor. The passage includes the proofs from the Quran (verse on highway robbers interpreted as imprisonment), Sunnah (the Prophet detained a man on suspicion), and Ijma' (consensus of the Companions). It also notes that the Prophet and the first three caliphs had no prison; 'Ali was the first to build one.

Key Terms
الحبس (al-habs): Imprisonment as a judicial measure to compel a debtor to pay or as a punishment for stubborn refusal.
الثمن (al-thaman): The sale price in a contract, which is a debt for which imprisonment is allowed if the buyer refuses to pay.
المهر المعجل (al-mahr al-mu'ajjal): The prompt dower that is due immediately in a marriage contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
For which of the following debts is a debtor NOT imprisoned if he claims poverty and the creditor cannot prove wealth?
A) Price of a sold item (thaman)
B) Loan (qard)
C) Prompt dower (mahr mu'ajjal)
D) Damages for usurpation (daman al-ghasb)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school allows imprisonment for a limited set of debts only when the debtor is proven wealthy and refuses to pay, with the duration left to the judge's discretion.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate
8 min
Imprisonment for Debt and Exceptional Cases
Ruling on imprisonment for debt and exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which Hanafi debts warrant imprisonment, explain the procedure when poverty is claimed, and identify the exceptions based on the type of debt.

Core Idea
Imprisonment is limited to contractual debts implying solvency; other debts require the creditor to prove wealth.

This lesson examines when a judge may imprison a debtor in Hanafi fiqh. The general rule is that imprisonment is a tool for collecting debts only when the debtor's solvency is presumed. The passage distinguishes between debts arising from contracts (mahr and kafalah) and those from tort or liability, and outlines the procedure for proving insolvency.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of debts that warrant imprisonment
From the text, note that imprisonment is allowed for the prompt dower (mahr mu'ajjal) and any debt undertaken by guarantee (kafalah). All other debts are excluded unless the creditor proves the debtor's wealth.
Contractual debts carry a presumption of solvency because the debtor voluntarily undertook them.
2
Understand the rule when the debtor claims poverty
If the debtor claims poverty (i'sar), he is not imprisoned immediately. Instead, the burden shifts to the creditor to prove the debtor's wealth. If proven, the judge may imprison; if not, the debtor is not imprisoned.
This applies only to the excluded 'other' debts. For mahr and kafalah, the debtor's poverty claim does not automatically stop imprisonment because solvency is presumed.
3
Analyze the judge's procedure after imprisonment
The judge imprisons the debtor for a period he determines (bima ra'a), based on circumstances. After that, he inquires about the debtor's condition from neighbors. If evidence of insolvency is presented, the debtor is released.
The duration is discretionary, not fixed. Narrations from Abu Hanifa suggesting fixed periods are not binding.
4
Recognize the proof of insolvency and exceptions
Evidence of insolvency can be established by a single just witness describing the debtor's straitened condition. The judge must release the debtor even against the creditor's will, unless the debt involves orphan's property, endowment (waqf), or an absent creditor.
This is based on the Quranic verse granting respite to the insolvent (Al-Baqarah: 280).

بيان الحبس
والمهر المعجل، وما التزمه بالكفالة لا في غيره إن ادّعى الفقر إلا أن يثبت غريمه غناه، فيحبسه بما رأى ثم يسأل عنه، فإن لم يظهر له مال، خلاه، والمهر المعجل، وما التزمه بالكفالة لا في غيره إن ادّعى الفقر إلا أن يثبت غريمه غناه، فيحبسه بما رأى ثم يسأل عنه، فإن لم يظهر له مال، خلاه.
والمهر: أي وفي كل مال التزمه مثل المهر إلخ. (عيني) وما التزمه بالكفالة [ أي وفي كل دين لزمه بعقد؛ لأنه بالإباء ظهر مطله . (عيني)] يعم الكفيل وكفيل الكفيل، وإن كثروا، ويعم الكفالة بالدرك، وفي كل عين يقدر على تسليمها ليشمل حبسه على العين المغصوبة والأمانات إذا امتنع الأمين من دفعها غير مدع هلاكها؛ لأنها صارت مغصوبة. (فتح) لا في غيره أي لا يحبسه في غير ذلك من الديون كضمان الغصب والمتلفات [وأرش الجنايات] وبدل عتق نصيب الشريك وديون النفقات للزوجة أو القريب، وإنما لا يحبس في هذه الأشياء إذا ادعى الفقر؛ لأنه لا دليل على اليسار؛ لأن دليل اليسار إذا لم يوجد كان القول لمن عليه الدين وعلى المدعي إثبات غناه أي قدرته على وفاء الدين، بخلاف الفصل الأول؛ لأنه حيث حصل المال في يده ثبت غناه به، وإقدامه على التزامه باختياره دليل يساره. (فتح) الفقر لأنه متمسك بالأصل وهو الفقر عند الأمر بالدفع. (عيني) غناه بدليل شرعي بأن له مالاً ( ط ) عيني) فيحبسه بما رأى [ أي فحينئذ يحبسه لظهور المطل. (عيني)] الباء للتعدية وهي ومدخولها متعلقة بمحذوف حال من الضمير المستتر في "فيحبسه"، و"ما" عبارة عن مدة وعائدها محذوف والتقدير: فيحبسه مقدرا بمدة رآها من المصلحة حتى يغلب على ظن القاضي أنه لو كان له مال لأظهره، ولم يصبر على مقاساة الحبس، وذلك يختلف باختلاف الشخص والزمان والمكان والمال، فلا معنى لتقديره وما روي عن أبي حنيفة أنه مقدر بشهر وعنه بستة أشهر، وعنه بأربعة أشهر فاتفاقي وليس بتقدير حتماً، والصحيح أن التقدير مفوض إلى رأي القاضي ولو يوماً، وعند بعض المالكية: في القليل لا يجب أكثر من نصف شهر، وفي الكثير أربعة أشهر فقط [ رمز الحقائق: ۱۲۱/۲]
:
ثم يسأل عنه: أي يسأل القاضي عن المحبوس من جيرانه احتياطاً لا وجوباً بعد ما حبسه قدر ما رآه، فإن قامت بينة على إعساره خلاه أي أخرجه من الحبس، ولا يحتاج فيه إلى لفظ الشهادة والعدل الواحد يكفي بغيبة دائن، والاثنان أحوط ولا يشترط حضرة الخصم وكيفيته أن يقول الشاهد: إن حاله حال المعسرين في نفقته وكسوته، وحاله ضيقة، وقد اختبرنا حاله في السر والعلانية رمز الحقائق: ١٢١/٢] (فتح) فإن لم يظهر له إلخ : أي أطلقه من الحبس جبراً على الدائن بلا أخذ كفيل إلا في ثلاث: مال يتيم ووقف وإذا كان الدائن غائبا؛ لأن عسرته ثبت عند القاضي واستحق النظرة إلى الميسرة؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِنْ كَانَ ذُو عُسْرَةٍ فَنَظِرَةٌ إِلَى مَيْسَرَةٍ (البقرة: ۲۸۰) فحبسه بعده يكون ظلما. (عيني، فتح)
خلاه: أي أخرجه من السجن بعد مضي المدة التي رآها في الحبس. (ط، عيني)
Statement on Imprisonment: And the prompt dower, and what he undertook by guarantee—not in other [debts] if he claims poverty, unless his creditor proves his wealth, then he imprisons him for as long as he sees fit, then he inquires about him, and if no wealth appears for him, he releases him. The dower: i.e., in every property he undertook like the dower etc. (Ayni) And what he undertook by guarantee [i.e., in every debt that became binding by contract; because by refusing, his delay became apparent. (Ayni)] includes the guarantor and the guarantor's guarantor, even if many, and includes the guarantee of recourse, and in every corporeal property that can be delivered, to include his imprisonment for a usurped property and trusts if the trustee refuses to deliver them not claiming their destruction; because they have become usurped. (Fath) Not in other: i.e., he does not imprison him in other than those debts, such as liability for usurpation and destroyed property [and blood-money for injuries] and the compensation for freeing a partner's share and debts of maintenance for wife or relative. He is not imprisoned in these things only if he claims poverty; because there is no evidence of solvency; because when evidence of solvency is not found, the statement is of the one who owes the debt, and the plaintiff must prove his wealth—i.e., his ability to pay the debt. Unlike the first section; because where property came into his hand, his wealth is established by it, and his undertaking it by choice is evidence of his solvency. (Fath) Poverty: because he adheres to the original [state] which is poverty when ordered to pay. (Ayni) His wealth by legal evidence that he has property. (T, Ayni) So he imprisons him for as long as he sees fit [i.e., then he imprisons him because his delay is apparent. (Ayni)] The ba is for transitive, and it and its object are attached to a deleted circumstantial clause from the implied pronoun in 'yahabisuhu', and 'ma' is an expression for a duration and its referent is deleted, the estimation: he imprisons him estimated for a duration he sees as in the interest until it overwhelms the judge's presumption that if he had wealth, he would have shown it and would not bear the hardship of imprisonment. That differs according to person, time, place and property, so there is no meaning to fixing it. What is narrated from Abu Hanifa that it is fixed to a month, and from him to six months, and from him to four months is coincidental and not a definite fixing. The correct is that fixing is delegated to the judge's opinion, even a day. According to some Malikiyyah: for little [debt], no more than half a month is necessary; for much, only four months. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 121/2] Then he inquires about him: i.e., the judge asks about the imprisoned person from his neighbors as a precaution, not obligatory, after he imprisons him as long as he saw fit. If evidence of his insolvency appears, he releases him, i.e., removes him from prison. There is no need for the wording of testimony, and one just witness suffices in the absence of the creditor; two are more precautionary. The presence of the opponent is not required. Its form is that the witness says: His condition is like the condition of the insolvent in his spending and clothing, his situation is straitened, and we have examined his condition in secret and openly [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 121/2] (Fath) If no [wealth] appears for him, etc.: i.e., he releases him from prison forcibly upon the creditor without taking a guarantor, except in three: property of an orphan, endowment, and when the creditor is absent; because his insolvency is established before the judge and he deserves respite until ease, due to the Almighty's saying: {And if someone is in hardship, then respite until ease} (Al-Baqarah: 280). Imprisoning him after that would be injustice. (Ayni, Fath) Khalahu: i.e., he removed him from prison after the passage of the period he had seen for imprisonment. (T, Ayni)
Source pages p. 412

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on imprisonment for debt. It begins by listing debts for which a debtor can be imprisoned: the prompt dower (mahr mu'ajjal) and any debt arising from a guarantee (kafalah). For these debts, if the debtor claims poverty, he is not imprisoned unless the creditor proves his wealth. If the creditor proves wealth, the judge imprisons him for a period determined by the judge's discretion (bima ra'a), then inquires about his condition. If no wealth appears, he is released. The commentary clarifies that 'what he undertook by guarantee' includes all debts that become binding by contract, including multiple guarantors and guarantee of recourse (kafalah bi al-darak). It also includes imprisonment for usurped property and trusts if the trustee refuses to deliver them. The exception ('not in other') refers to debts arising from liability for usurpation, destroying property, blood-money, compensation for freeing a partner's share, and maintenance debts for wife or relatives. For these, if the debtor claims poverty, he is not imprisoned because there is no presumption of solvency; the original state is poverty, and the creditor must prove wealth. The duration of imprisonment is not fixed but left to the judge's discretion, varying by person, time, place, and amount of debt. Narrations from Abu Hanifa suggesting a fixed period are coincidental. After the imprisonment period, the judge inquires about the debtor's condition from neighbors. Evidence of insolvency can be given by a single just witness in the creditor's absence; two are more precautionary. The witness describes the debtor's straitened circumstances. If insolvency is established, the judge must release the debtor forcibly, even over the creditor's objection, except in three cases: property of an orphan, endowment, and when the creditor is absent. This is based on the Quranic verse granting respite to the insolvent.

Key Terms
الحبس (al-habs): Imprisonment by the judge for debt collection.
المهر المعجل (al-mahr al-mu'ajjal): The dower paid promptly at marriage, not deferred.
الكفالة (al-kafalah): Guarantee; a contract creating a debt obligation.
الإعسار (al-i'sar): Insolvency; inability to pay debts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
For which debts can a debtor be imprisoned in Hanafi fiqh if he claims poverty?
A) Debts from liability for usurpation and destroyed property
B) Debts from maintenance of wife and relatives
C) The prompt dower and debts from guarantee (kafalah)
D) All debts without exception

Key Takeaway
Imprisonment for debt in Hanafi fiqh is limited to contractual debts (mahr and kafalah) where solvency is presumed; for other debts, the debtor's claim of poverty blocks imprisonment unless the creditor proves wealth.

Creditors' Right to Accompany Insolvent Debtor
Dispute on creditor accompaniment after insolvency release

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on whether the judge prevents creditors from accompanying the released insolvent debtor and explain the proof.

Core Idea
The judge does not prevent creditors from accompanying the debtor because divine respite is indefinite until ability to pay.

This lesson examines a key dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the rights of creditors after a debtor's release for insolvency. The practical consequence is whether creditors can monitor the debtor for new assets or must leave him alone.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the act in question: whether the judge should prevent creditors from accompanying the released insolvent debtor.
2
Note the dispute
Identify the Hanafi position (Imam Abu Hanifa: no prevention) and the opposing view (Sahibayn, Zufar, al-Shafi'i, Ahmad: prevention).
3
Analyze the opposing dalil
The opponents argue that divine respite (nazirah) is like a contractual term; creditors should not bother the debtor.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa argues respite is until ability to pay, which is possible at any moment, so creditors may accompany to prevent hiding assets.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The text states 'ind al-imam wa huwa al-sahih', so the fatwa is on Abu Hanifa's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم يحل بينه وبين غرمائه وردّ البينة على إفلاسه قبل حبسه، وبينة اليسار أحق، الموسر ويحبس الرجل لنفقة زوجته، لا في دين ولده
ولم يحل إلخ: أي لا يمنع القاضي الغرماء عن ملازمته عند الإمام، وهو الصحيح وقالا: يمنعهم؛ لأنه منظر بإنظار الله إلى الميسرة، فلو كان منظرا بإنظارهم بأن ضربوا له الأجل لا يكون لهم حق الملازمة قبل الأجل، فبإنظار الله تعالى أولى، وبه قال زفر والشافعي وأحمد وله أنه منظر إلى زمان قدرته على الإيفاء، وذلك ممكن في كل ساعة، فيلازمونه كي لا يخفيه. [رمز الحقائق: ١٢١/٢] (فتح، عناية) غرمائه أي لا يمنعهم من ملازمته فيلازمونه نهاراً لا ليلا (ط عيني ورد البينة: أي لو قامت البينة على إفلاسه قبل مضي المدة بأن أخبر اثنان أو شهد شاهدان أنه مفلس معدم لا نعلم له مالاً سوى كسوته التي عليه، وقد اختبرنا أمره سراً وعلانية، فلا يقبل القاضي هذه البينة في رواية؛ لأنها على النفي، فلا تقبل ما لم تتأيد بمؤيد، وقبل الحبس ما تأيدت، وإذا حبس، فمضت مدة، فقد تأيدت به؛ إذ الظاهر أن القادر على خلاص نفسه من مشقة الحبس لا يتحملها، وعلى هذه الرواية عامة المشايخ وفي رواية وهو المروي عن محمد: أنها تقبل قبل الحبس، وبه قال الشافعي وأحمد في رواية وبه كان يفتي الفقية أبو بكر محمد بن الفضل ونصير بن يحيى، وهو قول إسماعيل بن حماد بن أبي حنيفة. (عيني، عناية) وبينة اليسار أحق بالقبول من بينة إعساره] يعني إذا أقام المدعي البينة على اليسار، وأقام المدعى عليه على فكانت بينة اليسار أولى؛ لأن اليسار عارض والبينة للإثبات إلا أن يدعي المدعي اليسار ويقول المدعى
الإعسار،
عليه عسرت بعد ذلك وأقام بينة تقدم ؛ لأن معها علما بأمر حادث. (عيني، فتح) الموسر : أي إذا امتنع الغني عن إيفاء الحق مع القدرة عليه خلده في الحبس. (عيني) ويحبس الرجل إلخ: لأنه ظالم بالامتناع من الإنفاق بخلاف النفقة الماضية؛ لأنها تسقط بمضي الزمان (عيني)) أي إذا فرض القاضي على رجل نفقة زوجته أو اصطلحا على مقدار، فلم ينفق عليها، فرفعت إلى القاضي حبسه لظهور ظلمه بالامتناع، وإنما يتحقق الامتناع في اليوم الثاني من يوم فرضها، أما بمجرد فرضها لا يحبسه أما النفقة الماضية، فلا يحبس عليها وإن قضى بها إذا ادعى الفقر؛ لأنها ليست ببدل مال ولا التزمها بعقد.(فتح، عناية) لا في دين ولده [ أي لا يحبس الوالد في دين إلخ لأن الوالد لا يستحق العقوبة بسبب ولده. (عيني)] لأن الحبس نوع عقوبة، فلا يستحق الولد على والده كالحد والقصاص، والأصل في ذلك قوله تعالى: ﴿فَلا تَقُلْ لَهُمَا أُفٍّ وَلا تَنْهَرْهُمَا (الإسراء:۲۳) الآية، والمراد بالوالد: الأصل وإن علا، ولو جداً فاسداً، وبالولد: الفرع وإن سفل، وإذا لم يحبس فالقاضي يقضي دينه من ماله إن كان من جنسه، وإلا باعه لأداء الدين، والصحيح عندهما: بيع عقاره كمنقوله وكذا المولى لا يحبس بدين عبده المأذون إن لم يكن على العبد دين؛ لأن ماله للمولى، -
And he does not prevent between him and his creditors; and the evidence of his insolvency before his imprisonment is rejected; and evidence of solvency is more deserving. The wealthy [is imprisoned permanently]; and a man is imprisoned for the maintenance of his wife, not for the debt of his child. 'And he does not prevent' etc.: i.e., the judge does not prevent the creditors from accompanying him according to Imam [Abu Hanifa], and that is the correct view. They [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] said: He prevents them; because he is given respite by the respite of Allah until ease. If he were given respite by their respite—that they set a term for him—they would not have the right to accompany him before the term. So the respite of Allah is more entitled. Zufar, al-Shafi'i, and Ahmad also said this. And for him [Abu Hanifa] is that he is given respite until the time of his ability to pay, and that is possible at any moment, so they accompany him so that he does not hide [his property]. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 121/2] (Fath, 'Inayah) 'His creditors': i.e., he does not prevent them from accompanying him; so they accompany him by day, not by night. (T, Ayni) 'And the evidence is rejected': i.e., if evidence of his insolvency is established before the passage of the period—by two [persons] informing or two witnesses testifying that he is bankrupt, destitute, we do not know any property for him except his clothing that he is wearing, and we have examined his matter in secret and openly—the judge does not accept this evidence in one narration; because it is about a negative, so it is not accepted unless supported by a corroborating factor. And before imprisonment it is not supported. When he is imprisoned and a period passes, it is thereby supported; because the apparent is that one who is able to free himself from hardship of imprisonment would not bear it. According to this narration are the general mashayikh. In another narration—and it is the narration from Muhammad—that it is accepted before imprisonment. Al-Shafi'i and Ahmad in one narration also said this, and the faqih Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Fadl and Nasir ibn Yahya used to give fatwa according to it, and it is the saying of Isma'il ibn Hammad ibn Abi Hanifa. (Ayni, 'Inayah) 'And evidence of solvency is more deserving of acceptance than evidence of his insolvency': meaning if the plaintiff adduces evidence of solvency and the defendant adduces evidence of insolvency, the evidence of solvency is more deserving; because solvency is a supervening state, and evidence is for establishing [the original state], unless the plaintiff claims solvency and the defendant says I became insolvent after that and adduces evidence, then it is given precedence; because with it is knowledge of a new matter. (Ayni, Fath) 'The wealthy': i.e., if the wealthy person refuses to fulfill the right while able to, he imprisons him permanently. (Ayni) 'And a man is imprisoned' etc.: because he is a wrongdoer by refusing to spend, unlike past maintenance; because it is forfeited by passage of time. (Ayni) i.e., if the judge imposes on a man the maintenance of his wife, or they agree on an amount, then he does not spend on her, and she raises it to the judge, he imprisons him because his wrongdoing by refusal is apparent. Refusal is realized on the second day from the day of imposition; as for immediately after imposition, he does not imprison him. As for past maintenance, he is not imprisoned for it even if it is adjudicated, if he claims poverty; because it is not a substitute for property nor did he undertake it by contract. (Fath, 'Inayah) 'Not for the debt of his child': [i.e., the parent is not imprisoned for the debt of his child, etc., because the parent does not deserve punishment due to his child. (Ayni)] because imprisonment is a type of punishment, so the child does not deserve it on the parent, like hadd and qisas. The basis for this is the Almighty's saying: {So do not say to them 'uff' nor scold them} (Al-Isra': 23) and the verse. The intended meaning by 'parent' is the root [lineage] even if high, even an illegitimate grandfather; and by 'child' is the branch even if low. If he is not imprisoned, the judge pays his debt from his property if it is of the same type; otherwise he sells it to pay the debt. According to the correct view of the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad], the sale of his real estate is like his movable property. Similarly, the master is not imprisoned for the debt of his authorized slave if there is no debt upon the slave; because his property belongs to the master.
Source pages p. 413

Commentary
This passage continues the chapter on imprisonment, addressing several points. First, it discusses whether, after releasing an insolvent debtor, the judge should prevent other creditors from pursuing him. According to Imam Abu Hanifa (the correct view), the judge does not prevent creditors from accompanying the debtor (muwalat) so they can monitor him in case he acquires assets. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, along with Zufar, al-Shafi'i, and Ahmad, hold that the judge should prevent them because the debtor has been granted a divine respite until ease; thus, like a contractual term, creditors should not bother him. The Hanafi preference is that since the respite is indefinite until ability to pay is possible at any time, creditors may follow him day (but not night) to prevent him from hiding assets. Second, the passage addresses evidence of insolvency. If before imprisonment, witnesses testify that the debtor is bankrupt, this evidence is not accepted because it is negative and unsupported. After a period of imprisonment, such evidence is accepted because the debtor's endurance of imprisonment strongly indicates genuine insolvency. There is a narration from Muhammad al-Shaybani that evidence of insolvency is accepted even before imprisonment, which was followed by some later Hanafi scholars. Third, when competing evidence is presented—plaintiff proving solvency and defendant proving insolvency—the evidence of solvency is given precedence because solvency is a supervening condition, unless the defendant claims insolvency arose after the plaintiff's evidence. Fourth, if the debtor is wealthy (musir) and refuses to pay while able, he is imprisoned permanently until he pays. Fifth, a man is imprisoned for failing to pay ongoing court-ordered maintenance for his wife, because his refusal makes him a wrongdoer. Past maintenance, however, does not warrant imprisonment if he claims poverty, as it is not a contractual obligation. Sixth, a parent is not imprisoned for the debt of his child, because imprisonment is a punishment and the child does not deserve that against the parent, based on Quranic ethic of honoring parents. Instead, the judge sells the parent's property to pay the debt. Similarly, a master is not imprisoned for the debt of his authorized slave.

Key Terms
الملازمة (al-mulazamah): The act of creditors accompanying the debtor to keep track of his financial status.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi fatwa, what does the judge do regarding creditors accompanying a released insolvent debtor?
A) The judge prevents them from accompanying him.
B) The judge does not prevent them from accompanying him.
C) The judge allows accompaniment only at night.
D) The judge arrests the debtor again.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi judge does not prevent creditors from accompanying the released insolvent debtor, as the divine respite is indefinite.

Evidence of Insolvency: Before Imprisonment vs After
Ruling on acceptance of insolvency evidence relative to imprisonment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state when evidence of a debtor's insolvency is accepted according to the dominant Hanafi view and explain the reasoning.

Core Idea
Evidence of insolvency is rejected before imprisonment but accepted after a period of imprisonment.

This lesson examines the rules for accepting testimony that a debtor is insolvent. The dominant Hanafi view requires a period of imprisonment to corroborate the claim, while a minority view accepts it immediately. The reasoning involves the nature of negative evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the act: what evidence (bayyinah) of insolvency is being evaluated, and when it is accepted.
2
Understand the reasoning for rejection before imprisonment
The evidence is about a negative (lack of property); negative evidence is normally not accepted unless corroborated. Before imprisonment, there is no corroboration.
3
Understand acceptance after imprisonment
After a period of imprisonment, the debtor's willingness to endure hardship is seen as strong indication of genuine insolvency; thus the evidence is accepted.
4
Note the alternative narration
Imam Muhammad has a narration that evidence can be accepted even before imprisonment, followed by some later Hanafis.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The text says 'على هذه الرواية عامة المشايخ' (according to this narration are the general mashayikh), indicating the dominant view is rejection before imprisonment.

According to Imam Abu Hanifa (the correct view), the judge does not prevent creditors from accompanying the debtor (muwalat) so they can monitor him in case he acquires assets. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, along with Zufar, al-Shafi'i, and Ahmad, hold that the judge should prevent them because the debtor has been granted a divine respite until ease; thus, like a contractual term, creditors should not bother him. The Hanafi preference is that since the respite is indefinite until ability to pay is possible at any time, creditors may follow him day (but not night) to prevent him from hiding assets. Second, the passage addresses evidence of insolvency. If before imprisonment, witnesses testify that the debtor is bankrupt, this evidence is not accepted because it is negative and unsupported. After a period of imprisonment, such evidence is accepted because the debtor's endurance of imprisonment strongly indicates genuine insolvency. There is a narration from Muhammad al-Shaybani that evidence of insolvency is accepted even before imprisonment, which was followed by some later Hanafi scholars. Third, when competing evidence is presented—plaintiff proving solvency and defendant proving insolvency—the evidence of solvency is given precedence because solvency is a supervening condition, unless the defendant claims insolvency arose after the plaintiff's evidence. Fourth, if the debtor is wealthy (musir) and refuses to pay while able, he is imprisoned permanently until he pays. Fifth, a man is imprisoned for failing to pay ongoing court-ordered maintenance for his wife, because his refusal makes him a wrongdoer. Past maintenance, however, does not warrant imprisonment if he claims poverty, as it is not a contractual obligation. Sixth, a parent is not imprisoned for the debt of his child, because imprisonment is a punishment and the child does not deserve that against the parent, based on Quranic ethic of honoring parents. Instead, the judge sells the parent's property to pay the debt. Similarly, a master is not imprisoned for the debt of his authorized slave.

Key Terms
بينة الإفلاس (bayyinah al-iflas): Evidence proving the debtor's bankruptcy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the dominant Hanafi view, when is evidence of a debtor's insolvency accepted?
A) Immediately upon testimony, before any imprisonment
B) Only after the debtor has been imprisoned for a period
C) Only if the debtor confesses in court
D) Only if the creditor agrees

Key Takeaway
Evidence of insolvency is accepted only after a period of imprisonment, as this corroborates the claim.

Imprisonment for Maintenance: Present vs Past
Distinction between imprisonment for present and past maintenance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between imprisonment for present maintenance and past maintenance, and explain why past maintenance does not warrant imprisonment if poverty is claimed.

Core Idea
A man is imprisoned for failing to pay ongoing court-ordered maintenance, but not for past maintenance if he claims poverty.

This lesson clarifies the rules of imprisonment for non-payment of maintenance (nafaqah). The key distinction is between current maintenance, which is a continuing obligation, and past maintenance, which is forfeited by passage of time and does not justify imprisonment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
State the ruling: a man is imprisoned for failing to pay court-ordered maintenance for his wife.
The maintenance must be imposed by a judge or agreed upon.
2
Understand the reason for imprisonment
Refusal to pay ongoing maintenance is a form of wrongdoing (zulm), so imprisonment is justified.
3
Identify the exception
Past maintenance (al-nafaqah al-madiyah) does not lead to imprisonment if the husband claims poverty.
Past maintenance is not a contractual debt; it is forfeited by lapse of time.
4
Note the timing of refusal
Imprisonment is not immediate; it occurs on the second day after the court order, when refusal becomes apparent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم يحل بينه وبين غرمائه وردّ البينة على إفلاسه قبل حبسه، وبينة اليسار أحق، الموسر ويحبس الرجل لنفقة زوجته، لا في دين ولده
ولم يحل إلخ: أي لا يمنع القاضي الغرماء عن ملازمته عند الإمام، وهو الصحيح وقالا: يمنعهم؛ لأنه منظر بإنظار الله إلى الميسرة، فلو كان منظرا بإنظارهم بأن ضربوا له الأجل لا يكون لهم حق الملازمة قبل الأجل، فبإنظار الله تعالى أولى، وبه قال زفر والشافعي وأحمد وله أنه منظر إلى زمان قدرته على الإيفاء، وذلك ممكن في كل ساعة، فيلازمونه كي لا يخفيه. [رمز الحقائق: ١٢١/٢] (فتح، عناية) غرمائه أي لا يمنعهم من ملازمته فيلازمونه نهاراً لا ليلا (ط عيني ورد البينة: أي لو قامت البينة على إفلاسه قبل مضي المدة بأن أخبر اثنان أو شهد شاهدان أنه مفلس معدم لا نعلم له مالاً سوى كسوته التي عليه، وقد اختبرنا أمره سراً وعلانية، فلا يقبل القاضي هذه البينة في رواية؛ لأنها على النفي، فلا تقبل ما لم تتأيد بمؤيد، وقبل الحبس ما تأيدت، وإذا حبس، فمضت مدة، فقد تأيدت به؛ إذ الظاهر أن القادر على خلاص نفسه من مشقة الحبس لا يتحملها، وعلى هذه الرواية عامة المشايخ وفي رواية وهو المروي عن محمد: أنها تقبل قبل الحبس، وبه قال الشافعي وأحمد في رواية وبه كان يفتي الفقية أبو بكر محمد بن الفضل ونصير بن يحيى، وهو قول إسماعيل بن حماد بن أبي حنيفة. (عيني، عناية) وبينة اليسار أحق بالقبول من بينة إعساره] يعني إذا أقام المدعي البينة على اليسار، وأقام المدعى عليه على فكانت بينة اليسار أولى؛ لأن اليسار عارض والبينة للإثبات إلا أن يدعي المدعي اليسار ويقول المدعى
الإعسار،
عليه عسرت بعد ذلك وأقام بينة تقدم ؛ لأن معها علما بأمر حادث. (عيني، فتح) الموسر : أي إذا امتنع الغني عن إيفاء الحق مع القدرة عليه خلده في الحبس. (عيني) ويحبس الرجل إلخ: لأنه ظالم بالامتناع من الإنفاق بخلاف النفقة الماضية؛ لأنها تسقط بمضي الزمان (عيني)) أي إذا فرض القاضي على رجل نفقة زوجته أو اصطلحا على مقدار، فلم ينفق عليها، فرفعت إلى القاضي حبسه لظهور ظلمه بالامتناع، وإنما يتحقق الامتناع في اليوم الثاني من يوم فرضها، أما بمجرد فرضها لا يحبسه أما النفقة الماضية، فلا يحبس عليها وإن قضى بها إذا ادعى الفقر؛ لأنها ليست ببدل مال ولا التزمها بعقد.(فتح، عناية) لا في دين ولده [ أي لا يحبس الوالد في دين إلخ لأن الوالد لا يستحق العقوبة بسبب ولده. (عيني)] لأن الحبس نوع عقوبة، فلا يستحق الولد على والده كالحد والقصاص، والأصل في ذلك قوله تعالى: ﴿فَلا تَقُلْ لَهُمَا أُفٍّ وَلا تَنْهَرْهُمَا (الإسراء:۲۳) الآية، والمراد بالوالد: الأصل وإن علا، ولو جداً فاسداً، وبالولد: الفرع وإن سفل، وإذا لم يحبس فالقاضي يقضي دينه من ماله إن كان من جنسه، وإلا باعه لأداء الدين، والصحيح عندهما: بيع عقاره كمنقوله وكذا المولى لا يحبس بدين عبده المأذون إن لم يكن على العبد دين؛ لأن ماله للمولى، -
And he does not prevent between him and his creditors; and the evidence of his insolvency before his imprisonment is rejected; and evidence of solvency is more deserving. The wealthy [is imprisoned permanently]; and a man is imprisoned for the maintenance of his wife, not for the debt of his child. 'And he does not prevent' etc.: i.e., the judge does not prevent the creditors from accompanying him according to Imam [Abu Hanifa], and that is the correct view. They [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] said: He prevents them; because he is given respite by the respite of Allah until ease. If he were given respite by their respite—that they set a term for him—they would not have the right to accompany him before the term. So the respite of Allah is more entitled. Zufar, al-Shafi'i, and Ahmad also said this. And for him [Abu Hanifa] is that he is given respite until the time of his ability to pay, and that is possible at any moment, so they accompany him so that he does not hide [his property]. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 121/2] (Fath, 'Inayah) 'His creditors': i.e., he does not prevent them from accompanying him; so they accompany him by day, not by night. (T, Ayni) 'And the evidence is rejected': i.e., if evidence of his insolvency is established before the passage of the period—by two [persons] informing or two witnesses testifying that he is bankrupt, destitute, we do not know any property for him except his clothing that he is wearing, and we have examined his matter in secret and openly—the judge does not accept this evidence in one narration; because it is about a negative, so it is not accepted unless supported by a corroborating factor. And before imprisonment it is not supported. When he is imprisoned and a period passes, it is thereby supported; because the apparent is that one who is able to free himself from hardship of imprisonment would not bear it. According to this narration are the general mashayikh. In another narration—and it is the narration from Muhammad—that it is accepted before imprisonment. Al-Shafi'i and Ahmad in one narration also said this, and the faqih Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Fadl and Nasir ibn Yahya used to give fatwa according to it, and it is the saying of Isma'il ibn Hammad ibn Abi Hanifa. (Ayni, 'Inayah) 'And evidence of solvency is more deserving of acceptance than evidence of his insolvency': meaning if the plaintiff adduces evidence of solvency and the defendant adduces evidence of insolvency, the evidence of solvency is more deserving; because solvency is a supervening state, and evidence is for establishing [the original state], unless the plaintiff claims solvency and the defendant says I became insolvent after that and adduces evidence, then it is given precedence; because with it is knowledge of a new matter. (Ayni, Fath) 'The wealthy': i.e., if the wealthy person refuses to fulfill the right while able to, he imprisons him permanently. (Ayni) 'And a man is imprisoned' etc.: because he is a wrongdoer by refusing to spend, unlike past maintenance; because it is forfeited by passage of time. (Ayni) i.e., if the judge imposes on a man the maintenance of his wife, or they agree on an amount, then he does not spend on her, and she raises it to the judge, he imprisons him because his wrongdoing by refusal is apparent. Refusal is realized on the second day from the day of imposition; as for immediately after imposition, he does not imprison him. As for past maintenance, he is not imprisoned for it even if it is adjudicated, if he claims poverty; because it is not a substitute for property nor did he undertake it by contract. (Fath, 'Inayah) 'Not for the debt of his child': [i.e., the parent is not imprisoned for the debt of his child, etc., because the parent does not deserve punishment due to his child. (Ayni)] because imprisonment is a type of punishment, so the child does not deserve it on the parent, like hadd and qisas. The basis for this is the Almighty's saying: {So do not say to them 'uff' nor scold them} (Al-Isra': 23) and the verse. The intended meaning by 'parent' is the root [lineage] even if high, even an illegitimate grandfather; and by 'child' is the branch even if low. If he is not imprisoned, the judge pays his debt from his property if it is of the same type; otherwise he sells it to pay the debt. According to the correct view of the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad], the sale of his real estate is like his movable property. Similarly, the master is not imprisoned for the debt of his authorized slave if there is no debt upon the slave; because his property belongs to the master.

Commentary
This passage continues the chapter on imprisonment, addressing several points. First, it discusses whether, after releasing an insolvent debtor, the judge should prevent other creditors from pursuing him. According to Imam Abu Hanifa (the correct view), the judge does not prevent creditors from accompanying the debtor (muwalat) so they can monitor him in case he acquires assets. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, along with Zufar, al-Shafi'i, and Ahmad, hold that the judge should prevent them because the debtor has been granted a divine respite until ease; thus, like a contractual term, creditors should not bother him. The Hanafi preference is that since the respite is indefinite until ability to pay is possible at any time, creditors may follow him day (but not night) to prevent him from hiding assets. Second, the passage addresses evidence of insolvency. If before imprisonment, witnesses testify that the debtor is bankrupt, this evidence is not accepted because it is negative and unsupported. After a period of imprisonment, such evidence is accepted because the debtor's endurance of imprisonment strongly indicates genuine insolvency. There is a narration from Muhammad al-Shaybani that evidence of insolvency is accepted even before imprisonment, which was followed by some later Hanafi scholars. Third, when competing evidence is presented—plaintiff proving solvency and defendant proving insolvency—the evidence of solvency is given precedence because solvency is a supervening condition, unless the defendant claims insolvency arose after the plaintiff's evidence. Fourth, if the debtor is wealthy (musir) and refuses to pay while able, he is imprisoned permanently until he pays. Fifth, a man is imprisoned for failing to pay ongoing court-ordered maintenance for his wife, because his refusal makes him a wrongdoer. Past maintenance, however, does not warrant imprisonment if he claims poverty, as it is not a contractual obligation. Sixth, a parent is not imprisoned for the debt of his child, because imprisonment is a punishment and the child does not deserve that against the parent, based on Quranic ethic of honoring parents. Instead, the judge sells the parent's property to pay the debt. Similarly, a master is not imprisoned for the debt of his authorized slave.

Key Terms
النفقة الماضية (al-nafaqah al-madiyah): Past maintenance that was due but not paid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, for which type of maintenance is a man imprisoned if he fails to pay?
A) Both present and past maintenance
B) Present maintenance only, if he refuses
C) Past maintenance only
D) Neither, unless he is wealthy

Key Takeaway
Imprisonment for maintenance applies to present obligations; past maintenance does not warrant imprisonment if the husband claims poverty.

Parent's Exemption from Imprisonment for Child's Debt
Ruling exempting parents from imprisonment for child's debt, with Quranic proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that a parent is not imprisoned for the debt of his child and explain the textual proof from the Quran.

Core Idea
A parent is not imprisoned for his child's debt because imprisonment is a punishment, and children do not deserve to punish their parents.

This lesson addresses a specific case: can a parent be imprisoned for the debt of his child? The Hanafi ruling is clear: no. The proof is derived from the Quranic command to honor parents, which forbids even slight disrespect, implying a fortiori that severe punishment like imprisonment is prohibited.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State that a parent (including grandfathers) is not imprisoned for the debt of his child.
The parent is the root (al-asl) and the child is the branch (al-far').
2
Understand the reason
Imprisonment is a type of punishment ('uqubah). The child does not have the right to punish the parent, analogous to hadd and qisas.
3
Identify the dalil
The Quranic verse (Al-Isra': 23) prohibits even saying 'uff' to parents. This implies that any form of harm, especially imprisonment, is forbidden.
4
Know the alternative recourse
The judge does not leave the debt unpaid. Instead, he sells the parent's property to satisfy the debt.
If the parent's property is of a different type, the judge sells it to convert to cash.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, along with Zufar, al-Shafi'i, and Ahmad, hold that the judge should prevent them because the debtor has been granted a divine respite until ease; thus, like a contractual term, creditors should not bother him. The Hanafi preference is that since the respite is indefinite until ability to pay is possible at any time, creditors may follow him day (but not night) to prevent him from hiding assets. Second, the passage addresses evidence of insolvency. If before imprisonment, witnesses testify that the debtor is bankrupt, this evidence is not accepted because it is negative and unsupported. After a period of imprisonment, such evidence is accepted because the debtor's endurance of imprisonment strongly indicates genuine insolvency. There is a narration from Muhammad al-Shaybani that evidence of insolvency is accepted even before imprisonment, which was followed by some later Hanafi scholars. Third, when competing evidence is presented—plaintiff proving solvency and defendant proving insolvency—the evidence of solvency is given precedence because solvency is a supervening condition, unless the defendant claims insolvency arose after the plaintiff's evidence. Fourth, if the debtor is wealthy (musir) and refuses to pay while able, he is imprisoned permanently until he pays. Fifth, a man is imprisoned for failing to pay ongoing court-ordered maintenance for his wife, because his refusal makes him a wrongdoer. Past maintenance, however, does not warrant imprisonment if he claims poverty, as it is not a contractual obligation. Sixth, a parent is not imprisoned for the debt of his child, because imprisonment is a punishment and the child does not deserve that against the parent, based on Quranic ethic of honoring parents. Instead, the judge sells the parent's property to pay the debt. Similarly, a master is not imprisoned for the debt of his authorized slave.

Key Terms
الوالد (al-walid): Parent, including grandfather upward, even if illegitimate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which Quranic verse is cited as the basis for not imprisoning a parent for the child's debt?
A) Al-Baqarah: 280 (relief for debtor)
B) Al-Isra': 23 (honoring parents)
C) Al-Nisa': 58 (trusts)
D) Al-Ma'idah: 38 (theft punishment)

Key Takeaway
Parents are never imprisoned for their children's debts; instead, the judge sells their property.

Imprisonment for Debt and Maintenance: The Father's Exception and General Rules
Explanation of imprisonment with conditions for father and debtor.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a father is imprisoned for maintenance and distinguish the rules of imprisonment for debtors in Hanafi law.

Core Idea
A father is imprisoned only to prevent harm to his child, not for his own debts; debtors are imprisoned for creditors' rights unless they have hidden assets.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq with commentary explains the limits of imprisonment in Hanafi fiqh. It clarifies that a father is not imprisoned for mere indebtedness but only when he refuses to support his young or disabled child, drawing an analogy to self-defense. The text also differentiates between debt to third parties, debts of slaves, and debts of a mukatib.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle
The passage begins with an exception: the father is not imprisoned except if he refuses to spend. Note the word 'إلا إذا أبى' (except when he refuses). This sets the default that imprisonment is not allowed for a father unless specific conditions exist.
The phrase is 'لا يحبس الوالد إلا إذا أبى'.
2
Understand the condition for imprisoning the father
The commentary specifies the condition: the child must be young without property or an adult who is disabled (زمن). The harm caused by the father's refusal is destruction (إهلاك) of the child, which must be repelled. The analogy to self-defense (killing if attacked) shows the severity.
The condition is about preventing harm, not punishment.
3
Analyze the analogy (qiyas)
The author uses qiyas jaliy: just as one may kill an attacker to save life, one may imprison the father to save the child. This establishes that imprisonment is a means of preventing harm, not punishment for debt.
The analogy is explicit in the text: 'ألا ترى أن له أن يدفعه بقتله'.
4
Apply rules for other debtors
The text contrasts: a debtor is imprisoned for debts to third parties (ghurama') but a slave is not imprisoned for master's debt. A master can be imprisoned for mukatib's debt if different from kitabah type. A debtor with hidden property is not imprisoned. Note the nuances: the mukatib is treated as free for earnings, and setoff (muqassa) occurs for same type.
The phrase 'ولا يحبس المديون إذا كان له مال غائب' indicates hidden property prevents imprisonment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Book of Judgments, 413. Explanation of imprisonment: except when he refuses to spend on him, and Allah knows best. That is, the father refuses. And if he has a debt, he is imprisoned; because this imprisonment is for the right of creditors, and they are strangers. The slave is not imprisoned for the master's debt, because no debt is required of him. The master is imprisoned for the debt of his mukatib if it is not of the same type as the kitabah payment; because the mukatib is like a free person regarding his earnings. Its type is not imprisoned because setoff occurs. The debtor is not imprisoned if he has hidden property or [if] he is imprisoned for his sake [as master?], even if the debtor is wealthy. ('Ayni, Fath) From 'except when he refuses': meaning the parent is not imprisoned except when he refuses to spend on the child, then he is imprisoned. This is understood when the child is young with no property, or an adult who is disabled; because by refusing he intends to destroy him, so he is imprisoned to repel destruction from him. Do you not see that he can repel him by killing him if he draws a sword and he cannot repel him except by killing him. Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 121/2] (Fath, 'Inayah)
Source pages p. 414

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the rulings of imprisonment in Hanafi fiqh. It begins by stating the general principle: a father is not imprisoned except when he refuses to spend on his child. The commentary clarifies that this applies when the child is a minor with no property or an adult who is disabled, because the father's refusal would lead to harm. It draws an analogy (qiyas jaliy) with the right to kill if attacked with a sword. Then it discusses imprisonment for debt: a debtor is imprisoned for debts to third parties (ghurama'), but a slave is not imprisoned for the master's debt. A master can be imprisoned for the debt of his mukatib (slave under contract of manumission) if the debt is not of the same type as the kitabah payment, because the mukatib is like a free person in his earnings. A debtor with hidden assets or a wealthy debtor may still be imprisoned according to some authorities.

Key Terms
الحبس (al-habs): Imprisonment as a legal penalty to compel fulfillment of a duty, such as child support or debt repayment.
الوالد (al-walid): Father; in this context, a parent who refuses to support his child.
مكاتب (mukatib): A slave who has entered a contract of kitabah with his master to earn his freedom by paying installments.

Key Terms from Source Passage

The Ruling on a Judge's Letter: Acceptance Conditions and Proof
Ruling with proof: acceptance of judge's letter and exception for hadd/qisas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions for accepting a judge's letter (official judge, non-hadd/qisas, valid testimony) and explain the Hanafi proof from the narration of 'Ali (ra).

Core Idea
A judge's letter is accepted in all financial and personal rights except hadd and qisas, as a necessity-based concession overriding qiyas.

This lesson examines the foundational ruling on a judge's written verdict sent to another judge. Although analogical reasoning (qiyas) would reject such letters due to risk of forgery, the Hanafi school accepts them based on the precedent of 'Ali (ra) and public need. We will explore the conditions for acceptance and the important exception of hadd and qisas punishments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is writing and accepting a judge's letter. Its ruling is permissible (mubah) as a concession.
It is not obligatory, but a dispensation for necessity.
2
State the conditions for acceptance
The writer must be an official judge appointed by the Imam (not a muhakkam); the letter must concern rights other than hadd and qisas; and the witnesses must testify against a present defendant.
These conditions distinguish valid letters from invalid ones.
3
Locate the primary proof
The narration that 'Ali (ra) permitted it due to people's need is the primary proof.
The text says: 'لما روي أن علياً أجاز ذلك؛ لحاجة الناس إليه'.
4
Analyze the qiyas objection
Qiyas would reject the letter because oral testimony of the writer is not accepted, and there is risk of forgery. The Hanafi response is that necessity overrides qiyas.
This shows the role of istihsan and necessity in Hanafi jurisprudence.
5
Note the cross-school disagreement
Imam Malik (in one narration) allows letters in hadd and qisas as well, but the Hanafi school rejects that.
The disagreement is based on different weight given to the doubt of forgery.

Source Text

Chapter of a judge's letter to another judge, etc. Chapter of a judge's letter. And the judge writes to the judge in matters other than hadd and qisas. If they testify against a defendant, he judges by the testimony, i.e. the witnesses. Chapter of a judge's letter etc. [ i.e. in explanation of the rulings of a judge's written message to another judge, etc. ('Ayni)] Know that writing with his knowledge is like judging with his knowledge in the most sound opinion. And a judge's letter is not accepted from a muhakkam (arbitrator), but from a judge appointed by the Imam who has the authority to perform Friday prayer. And it is said: it is accepted from a judge of a rural district to a judge of a city or rural district. And if the letter that came to him is for someone whose testimony is not accepted for him, like parents and wife, then it is permissible to judge by it, unlike if they had come to him without a letter. And his statement: 'in other than hadd and qisas' - the excluded thing is omitted, i.e. the judge writes in all rights that are established despite doubt and are not invalidated by doubt, such as debt, marriage, divorce, pre-emption, manumission, agency, bequest, death, inheritance, killing that necessitates monetary compensation, lineage from the living and the dead, usurpation, denied trusts like deposits, partnerships, loans, movable objects like a slave or slave-girl, and immovable like real estate if its four boundaries are specified. And that is narrated from Muhammad, and the later scholars rely on it, and it is what is given as fatwa due to necessity. In the apparent transmission (zahir al-riwaya), it is not accepted for immovable objects and is accepted for movable objects, due to the need to refer to them at the time of claim and testimony, unlike real estate and other rights. And from Abu Yusuf: he accepts it for male slaves but not female slaves, due to the prevalence of absconding among them without the female slaves. Then the letter to the judge is of two types: one is the sijill (official record), and the second is called the hukmi (judgmental) letter, as he explained with his statement: 'if they testify' etc. Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 122/2] (Fath, 'Inayah) 'Other than hadd': what is meant by 'other than hadd and qisas' is the rights that are established despite doubts, and they (hadd and qisas) are repelled by doubts. ('Inayah) 'Against a present opponent after the plaintiff's claim and the defendant's denial.' (Ma'din) 'By the testimony': i.e. by the obligation of the testified matter upon the defendant for the plaintiff. ('Ayni)
Source pages p. 415

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the chapter of a judge writing to another judge. It first clarifies that a judge's written verdict (kitab al-qadi) is accepted only from a properly appointed judge (who leads Friday prayer), not from a voluntary arbitrator (muhakkam). The letter is not accepted in hadd and qisas cases due to the principle of repelling punishments by doubts. However, it is accepted in all other financial and personal rights, including debts, marriage, divorce, pre-emption, etc. The commentator explains that the practice of accepting such letters is a concession due to people's need, based on the precedent of 'Ali (ra). He also discusses the disagreement with Imam Malik, who allowed it in hadd and qisas. Within the Hanafi school, there is a difference: in the apparent transmission (zahir al-riwaya), letters are not accepted for immovable property, but later scholars (mutakkhirin) accepted for both movable and immovable due to necessity. Abu Yusuf had a separate opinion about male vs. female slaves. The passage also distinguishes between two types of letters: the sijill (official record) and the hukmi letter.

Key Terms
كتاب القاضي (kitab al-qadi): A written verdict or communication sent by one judge to another judge regarding a legal case.
حد وقود (hadd wa qisas): Fixed corporal punishments (hadd) and retributive justice (qisas); both are repelled by doubts in Hanafi law.
محكم (muhakkam): A private arbitrator appointed by disputing parties, not an official judge (qadi). His letter is not accepted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A judge's letter is a necessity-based concession accepted in all rights except hadd and qisas, which are repelled by doubt.

Intra-Hanafi Differences: Property Types, Distance, and the Mufta Bihi
Expansion of ruling: intra-Hanafi differences on property and distance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the difference between the zahir al-riwaya and later Hanafi positions on accepting letters for immovable property, and correctly apply the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Later Hanafi scholars accepted judges' letters for both movable and immovable property due to necessity, overriding the earlier restriction to movables only.

While the Hanafi school generally accepts judges' letters in non-hadd cases, there are important internal differences regarding the types of property covered. The earliest transmitted opinion (zahir al-riwaya) limited acceptance to movable property, but later scholars expanded it to immovable property as well due to practical necessity. Understanding this evolution is crucial for correct fatwa practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
What types of property can be included in a judge's letter?
The dispute is within the Hanafi school, not between schools.
2
State the zahir al-riwaya position
Only movable property (manqulat) is accepted; immovable (ghayr manqula) is not.
This is the apparent transmission in the six core books.
3
Note Abu Yusuf's refinement
He accepted for male slaves but not female slaves due to risk of absconding.
This shows attention to specific circumstances.
4
Explain the later view
Both movable and immovable are accepted, as narrated from Muhammad, and relied upon by later scholars (mutakkhirin) due to necessity.
The text says: 'وعليه المتأخرون، وهو الذي يفتى به للضرورة'.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The later view is the operative position for fatwa. Also note the distance condition: Abu Yusuf accepts for short distances if return is not possible same day.
Be aware of these differences for historical understanding, but follow the mufta bihi in practice.

(عيني)] اعلم أن الكتاب بعلمه كالقضاء بعلمه في الأصح ولا يقبل كتاب القاضي من محكم بل من قاض مولى من قبل الإمام يملك إقامة الجمعة، وقيل: يقبل من قاضي رستاق إلى قاضي مصر أو رستاق وإذا كان الكتاب الذي ورد عليه لمن لا تقبل شهادته له كالوالدين والزوجة جاز القضاء به، بخلاف ما إذا ترافعوا إليه من غير كتاب. وأورد هذا الباب بعد فصل الحبس؛ لأن الحبس يتم بقاض واحد وكتاب القاضي إلى القاضي لا يتم إلا بقاضيين والواحد قبل المتعدد لا محالة، كتاب القاضي إلى القاضي فيما دون مسيرة السفر لا يجوز في ظاهر الرواية، وعن أبي يوسف: أنه لو كان بحال لو غدا إلى باب القاضي لا يمكنه الرجوع إلى منزله في يومه ذلك، يقبل، وعليه الفتوى.(مسكين، فتح) وغيره : أي غير كتاب القاضي والمراد به قوله وتقضي المرأة" إلخ. (مسكين، فتح) ويكتب القاضي إلخ في غير حد وقود، والقياس يأبى جواز العمل بهذا الكتاب؛ لأنه لا يكون أقوى من ألفاظ الكاتب، ولو حضر الكاتب بنفسه في مجلس المكتوب إليه، وعبر بلسانه ما في الكتاب لم يعمل به القاضي فكيف بالكتاب؟ ولأن فيه شبهة التزوير؛ إذ الخط يشبه الخط، والخاتم يشبه الخاتم، إلا أنه جوز لحاجة الناس؛ لما روي أن علياً أجاز ذلك؛ لحاجة الناس إليه. [ تبيين الحقائق: ٩٦/٥] وهذه المسألة بالإجماع إلا في رواية عن مالك: أنه يكتب القاضي في الحدود والقود أيضاً، وإنما لم يقبل في الحد والقود أي القصاص؛ لما فيه من الشبهة وهما يندرءان بها. وقوله: "في غير حد وقود المستثنى منه محذوف أي يكتب القاضي في كل الحقوق التي تثبت مع الشبهة ولا تسقط بها كالدين والنكاح والطلاق والشفعة والعتاق والوكالة والوصية والوفاة والوراثة والقتل الذي موجبه المال، والنسب من الحي ،والميت والغصب والأمانة المجحودة من وديعة ومضاربة وعارية والأعيان المنقولة كالعبد والجارية، وغير المنقولة كالعقار إذا بين حدوده الأربع، ويروى ذلك عن محمد، وعليه المتأخرون، وهو الذي يفتى به للضرورة، وفي ظاهر الرواية لا يقبل في الأعيان الغير المنقولة ويقبل في المنقول؛ للحاجة إلى الإشارة إليها عند الدعوى والشهادة بخلاف العقار وغيرها من الحقوق وعن أبي يوسف أنه يقبل في العبيد دون الإماء؛ لغلبة الإباق فيهم دون الإماء، ثم الكتاب إلى القاضي نوعان: أحدهما: السجل والثاني يسمى بالكتاب الحكمي كما بينه بقوله: "فإن شهدوا" إلخ. رمز الحقائق: ١٢٢/٢] (فتح، عناية) غير حد: المراد بغير الحد والقود الحقوق التي تثبت بالشبهات وهما يندرءان بالشبهات. (عناية) على خصم حاضر بعد دعوى المدعي وإنكار المدعى عليه. (معدن) بالشهادة: أي بلزوم المشهود به على المدعى عليه للمدعي. (عيني)
Chapter of a judge's letter to another judge, etc. Chapter of a judge's letter. And the judge writes to the judge in matters other than hadd and qisas. If they testify against a defendant, he judges by the testimony, i.e. the witnesses. Chapter of a judge's letter etc. [ i.e. in explanation of the rulings of a judge's written message to another judge, etc. ('Ayni)] Know that writing with his knowledge is like judging with his knowledge in the most sound opinion. And a judge's letter is not accepted from a muhakkam (arbitrator), but from a judge appointed by the Imam who has the authority to perform Friday prayer. And it is said: it is accepted from a judge of a rural district to a judge of a city or rural district. And if the letter that came to him is for someone whose testimony is not accepted for him, like parents and wife, then it is permissible to judge by it, unlike if they had come to him without a letter. And this chapter is placed after the section on imprisonment because imprisonment is completed by one judge, while a judge's letter to a judge is not completed except by two judges, and the one comes before the multiple necessarily. A judge's letter for a distance less than that of travel is not permissible in the apparent transmission (zahir al-riwaya), and from Abu Yusuf: if it were such that if he went to the judge's door he could not return to his home in that same day, then it is accepted, and on that is the fatwa. (Miskin, Fath) And 'etc.' means other than the judge's letter, and what is meant by it is his statement 'and a woman judges' etc. (Miskin, Fath) And the judge writes etc. in other than hadd and qisas. Analogy (qiyas) rejects the permissibility of acting on this letter, because it is not stronger than the words of the writer. If the writer himself had come to the court of the addressee and verbally expressed what is in the letter, the judge would not act on it, so how about the letter? And because there is the possibility of forgery in it, since handwriting resembles handwriting, and seals resemble seals. However, it was permitted due to people's need; because it was narrated that 'Ali permitted it due to people's need. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: 96/5] And this issue is by consensus except for a narration from Malik: that the judge writes in hadd and qisas as well. And it is not accepted in hadd and qisas, i.e. retaliation, because of the doubt (shubha) in them, and they are repelled by doubts. And his statement: 'in other than hadd and qisas' - the excluded thing is omitted, i.e. the judge writes in all rights that are established despite doubt and are not invalidated by doubt, such as debt, marriage, divorce, pre-emption, manumission, agency, bequest, death, inheritance, killing that necessitates monetary compensation, lineage from the living and the dead, usurpation, denied trusts like deposits, partnerships, loans, movable objects like a slave or slave-girl, and immovable like real estate if its four boundaries are specified. And that is narrated from Muhammad, and the later scholars rely on it, and it is what is given as fatwa due to necessity. In the apparent transmission (zahir al-riwaya), it is not accepted for immovable objects and is accepted for movable objects, due to the need to refer to them at the time of claim and testimony, unlike real estate and other rights. And from Abu Yusuf: he accepts it for male slaves but not female slaves, due to the prevalence of absconding among them without the female slaves. Then the letter to the judge is of two types: one is the sijill (official record), and the second is called the hukmi (judgmental) letter, as he explained with his statement: 'if they testify' etc. Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 122/2] (Fath, 'Inayah) 'Other than hadd': what is meant by 'other than hadd and qisas' is the rights that are established despite doubts, and they (hadd and qisas) are repelled by doubts. ('Inayah) 'Against a present opponent after the plaintiff's claim and the defendant's denial.' (Ma'din) 'By the testimony': i.e. by the obligation of the testified matter upon the defendant for the plaintiff. ('Ayni)
Source pages p. 415

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the chapter of a judge writing to another judge. It first clarifies that a judge's written verdict (kitab al-qadi) is accepted only from a properly appointed judge (who leads Friday prayer), not from a voluntary arbitrator (muhakkam). The letter is not accepted in hadd and qisas cases due to the principle of repelling punishments by doubts. However, it is accepted in all other financial and personal rights, including debts, marriage, divorce, pre-emption, etc. The commentator explains that the practice of accepting such letters is a concession due to people's need, based on the precedent of 'Ali (ra). He also discusses the disagreement with Imam Malik, who allowed it in hadd and qisas. Within the Hanafi school, there is a difference: in the apparent transmission (zahir al-riwaya), letters are not accepted for immovable property, but later scholars (mutakkhirin) accepted for both movable and immovable due to necessity. Abu Yusuf had a separate opinion about male vs. female slaves. The passage also distinguishes between two types of letters: the sijill (official record) and the hukmi letter.

Key Terms
كتاب القاضي (kitab al-qadi): A written verdict or communication sent by one judge to another judge regarding a legal case.
حد وقود (hadd wa qisas): Fixed corporal punishments (hadd) and retributive justice (qisas); both are repelled by doubts in Hanafi law.
محكم (muhakkam): A private arbitrator appointed by disputing parties, not an official judge (qadi). His letter is not accepted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school's mufta bihi (operative position), is a judge's letter accepted for immovable property?
A) Yes, based on necessity.
B) No, only movable property is accepted.
C) Yes, but only if boundaries are not specified.
D) No, because land cannot be transferred by letter.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's operative position accepts judges' letters for both movable and immovable property, overruling the earlier restriction due to necessity.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate
10 min
The Judge's Letter: Ruling, Conditions, and Types
Explains ruling, conditions, and types of a judge's letter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on a judge's letter, identify conditions for its validity, explain the exception for hudud and qisas, and distinguish between a sijill and a kitab hukmi.

Core Idea
A judge's letter is an exception to qiyas, accepted by necessity, but not in hudud and qisas which are averted by doubts.

This lesson examines the complex topic of judicial correspondence in Hanafi fiqh. While analogical reasoning (qiyas) would reject it due to risk of forgery, the practice is allowed due to people's need. We will explore the conditions for validity, the exceptions for hudud and qisas, the intra-Hanafi differences on distance and immovable property, and the crucial distinction between the two types of letters: the sijill (post-judgment record) and the kitab hukmi (testimony transmission).

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic ruling and its justification
Determine that the judge's letter is permissible (ja'iz) as an exception to qiyas, supported by the action of Ali and the principle of necessity.
The text explicitly rejects qiyas due to forgery risk but permits by istihsan.
2
Determine the conditions for the writing judge
The letter must come from a properly appointed judge (not an arbitrator) who has authority to lead Friday prayer.
3
Analyze the distance requirement and intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
In zahir al-riwaya, the distance must be travel distance; Abu Yusuf accepts if return within a day is impossible; the mufta bihi is the latter.
4
Recognize the exception for hudud and qisas
The letter is not accepted in hadd and qisas cases because they are averted by doubts (shubuhat). This is consensus except a narration from Malik.
The shubha in the letter (possible forgery) is sufficient to block enforcement.
5
Distinguish between sijill and kitab hukmi
The sijill is a record of a judgment already passed, binding on the addressee judge. The kitab hukmi transmits testimony before judgment and is not binding; the addressee may adjudicate independently.
Sijill = after judgment, kitab hukmi = before judgment.
