باب كتاب القاضي إلى القاضي وغيره
ويكتب القاضي إلى القاضي في غير حدّ وقود، فإن شهدوا على خصم، حكم بالشهادة أي الشهود
اعلم أن الكتاب بعلمه كالقضاء بعلمه في الأصح ولا يقبل كتاب القاضي من محكم بل من قاض مولى من قبل الإمام يملك إقامة الجمعة، وقيل: يقبل من قاضي رستاق إلى قاضي مصر أو رستاق وإذا كان الكتاب الذي ورد عليه لمن لا تقبل شهادته له كالوالدين والزوجة جاز القضاء به، بخلاف ما إذا ترافعوا إليه من غير كتاب. وأورد هذا الباب بعد فصل الحبس؛ لأن الحبس يتم بقاض واحد وكتاب القاضي إلى القاضي لا يتم إلا بقاضيين والواحد قبل المتعدد لا محالة، كتاب القاضي إلى القاضي فيما دون مسيرة السفر لا يجوز في ظاهر الرواية، وعن أبي يوسف: أنه لو كان بحال لو غدا إلى باب القاضي لا يمكنه الرجوع إلى منزله في يومه ذلك، يقبل، وعليه الفتوى.(مسكين، فتح) وغيره : أي غير كتاب القاضي والمراد به قوله وتقضي المرأة" إلخ. (مسكين، فتح) ويكتب القاضي إلخ في غير حد وقود، والقياس يأبى جواز العمل بهذا الكتاب؛ لأنه لا يكون أقوى من ألفاظ الكاتب، ولو حضر الكاتب بنفسه في مجلس المكتوب إليه، وعبر بلسانه ما في الكتاب لم يعمل به القاضي فكيف بالكتاب؟ ولأن فيه شبهة التزوير؛ إذ الخط يشبه الخط، والخاتم يشبه الخاتم، إلا أنه جوز لحاجة الناس؛ لما روي أن علياً أجاز ذلك؛ لحاجة الناس إليه. [ تبيين الحقائق: ٩٦/٥] وهذه المسألة بالإجماع إلا في رواية عن مالك: أنه يكتب القاضي في الحدود والقود أيضاً، وإنما لم يقبل في الحد والقود أي القصاص؛ لما فيه من الشبهة وهما يندرءان بها. وقوله: "في غير حد وقود المستثنى منه محذوف أي يكتب القاضي في كل الحقوق التي تثبت مع الشبهة ولا يسقط بها كالدين والنكاح والطلاق والشفعة والعتاق والوكالة والوصية والوفاة والوراثة والقتل الذي موجبه المال، والنسب من الحي ،والميت والغصب والأمانة المجحودة من وديعة ومضاربة وعارية والأعيان المنقولة كالعبد والجارية، وغير المنقولة كالعقار إذا بين حدوده الأربع، ويروى ذلك عن محمد، وعليه المتأخرون، وهو الذي يفتى به للضرورة، وفي ظاهر الرواية لا يقبل في الأعيان الغير المنقولة ويقبل في المنقول؛ للحاجة إلى الإشارة إليها عند الدعوى والشهادة بخلاف العقار وغيرها من الحقوق وعن أبي يوسف أنه يقبل في العبيد دون الإماء؛ لغلبة الإباق فيهم دون الإماء، ثم الكتاب إلى القاضي نوعان: أحدهما: السجل والثاني يسمى بالكتاب الحكمي كما بينه بقوله: "فإن شهدوا" إلخ.
غير حد: المراد بغير الحد والقود الحقوق التي تثبت بالشبهات وهما يندرءان بالشبهات. على خصم حاضر بعد دعوى المدعي وإنكار المدعى عليه. بالشهادة: أي بلزوم المشهود به على المدعى عليه للمدعي.
وكتب بحكمه وهو المدعو سجلاً، وإلا لم يحكم، وكتب الشهادة ليحكم المكتوم الكتاب الذي فيه الحكم القاضي ا الكاتب إليه بها، وهو الكتاب الحكمي، وهو نقل الشهادة في الحقيقة الشهادة أي الكتاب الحكمي يسمى أي القاضي سجلاً؛ لأنه سجله وكتب بحكمه: وإنما يكتب السجل حتى لا ينسى الواقعة على طول الزمان وليكون الكتاب مذكراً لها، وإلا فلا يحتاج إلى كتابة الحكم؛ لأنه قد تم بحضور الخصم نفسه أو من يقوم مقامه، إلا إذا غاب بعد الحكم عليه أو جحد الحكم، فحينئذ يكتب ليستوفي منه الحق أو لينفذ حكمه، وقوله: "وهو المدعو سجلاً"، سياق هذا الكلام يوهم انحصار إطلاق السجل على مكتوب ثبت حكمه بشهادة الشهود مع أنه لو ثبت الحكم بالإقرار وكتب بالحكم فذلك أيضاً سجل، فالمراد: أن الحجة التي فيها حكم القاضي يدعى سجلا في عرفهم. سجلاً : أي : أي أحكمه بالحكم، فالسجل لا يكون إلا بعد الحكم. وإلا: أي وإن لم يكن الخصم يعني المدعى عليه حاضرا. لم يحكم أي القاضي الكاتب بالشهادة؛ لأن الحكم على الغائب لا يجوز. الحكمي نسبته إلى الحكم باعتبار المآل وليس بسجل. نقل الشهادة: أي الكتاب الحكمي نقل الشهادة والفرق بينه وبين السجل أن السجل لا يكون إلا بعد الحكم، والكتاب الحكمي لا يكون إلا قبل الحكم، وحكم القاضي في السجل إذا وقع في مسألة مختلف فيها ليس للمكتوب إليه ولاية الرد بل عليه تنفيذه؛ لاتصال الحكم به، بخلاف الكتاب الحكمي، فإنه جاز للمكتوب إليه مخالفة رأي الكاتب ونقض حكمه، وقد ذكر كيفية الكتاب الحكمي أنه يكتب هكذا: من قاضي بخارا إلى قاضي سمرقند أن فلاناً وفلاناً شهدا عندي أن العبد الفلاني المسمى بمبارك الذي حليته كذا وكذا، وسنه وقيمته مالکه فلان، ووقع بسمرقند في يد فلان إلى آخر الكتاب ويختمه، فإذا وصل إلى قاضي من كذا، أبق . منه سمر قند كفيلاً يحضر الخصم مع العبد، ويفتح الكتاب بشرائطه التي في المتن فإن لم تكن حليته كما كتب يتركه. وإن كان فالخصم إن ذهب إلى بخارا ،فبها وإلا يسلم العبد إلى المدعي لا على وجه القضاء، ويأخذ بنفس العبد، ويجعل بعنقه خاتماً من رصاص، ويختمه حتى لا يتعرض له أحد في الطريق أنه سرق، ويكتب إلى قاضي بخارا جواب ،كتابه وأنه أرسل إليه حكم العبد، فإذا وصل إليه الكتاب يحضر الشهود الذين شهدوا في غيبة العبد ليشهدوا في حضرته فيشيروا إليه أنه ملك المدعي، لكن لا يحكم بل يكتب هو إلى قاضي سمرقند أن الشهود شهدوا بحضوره ه، وأرسله مع العبد إليه؛ ليحكم القاضي بسمرقند على الخصم ويبرأ الكفيل عن " يشترط أن يكون الكتاب عن قاض معلوم إلى قاض معلوم، في أمر ،معلوم لمدع ،معلوم على مدعى عليه معلوم، وأعلام هؤلاء بذكر اسمهم ونسبهم إلى أبيهم وجدهم أو قبيلتهم، فإن لم يذكر اسم الأب ولا الجد، لا يحصل التعريف إلا إذا كان مشهوراً باسمه العلم.
في الحقيقة لأن القاضي الكاتب لم يحكم بالشهادة وإنما نقلها إلى المكتوب إليه ليحكم بها.
كفالته، ثم
Chapter on the Judge's Letter to Another Judge and Others
and the judge writes to another judge in other than hadd and qisas, and if they testify against a defendant, he judges by the testimony, i.e. the witnesses.
Know that writing based on his knowledge is like judging based on his knowledge in the soundest view, and the letter of a judge is not accepted from an arbitrator but only from a judge appointed by the Imam who has the authority to lead Friday prayer, and it is said: it is accepted from a judge of a district to a judge of a major city or district. And if the letter received concerns someone whose testimony is not accepted for him, like parents and wife, it is permissible to judge by it, unlike if they come to him without a letter. And this chapter was placed after the chapter on imprisonment because imprisonment is completed by one judge, while a judge's letter to a judge is not completed except by two judges, and the single comes before the multiple inevitably. The judge's letter to a judge within less than travel distance is not permissible in the apparent transmission, and from Abu Yusuf: if he were in a state that if he went in the morning to the door of the judge he could not return to his home that day, it is accepted, and the fatwa is upon it. (Miskeen, Fath) and other than that: meaning other than the judge's letter, and what is meant by it is his saying: 'and the woman judges' etc. (Miskeen, Fath) And the judge writes etc. in other than hadd and qisas. Analogy would reject the permissibility of acting upon this letter because it is not stronger than the words of the writer, and if the writer himself came to the court of the addressee and expressed orally what is in the letter, the judge would not act upon it, so how about the letter? And because there is a suspicion of forgery, as one handwriting resembles another and one seal resembles another, except that it was permitted due to people's need; because it was narrated that Ali permitted that due to people's need. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: 5/96] And this matter is by consensus except for a narration from Malik: that the judge writes in hadd and qisas as well. And the reason it is not accepted in hadd and qisas, i.e. retribution, is due to the doubt in it, and both are averted by doubts. And His statement: 'in other than hadd and qisas', the excepted part is omitted, meaning that the judge writes in all rights that are established with doubt and are not nullified by it, such as debt, marriage, divorce, pre-emption, manumission, agency, will, death, inheritance, killing that requires monetary compensation, lineage from the living and the dead, usurpation, denied trust such as deposit, mudaraba, loan, movable items such as a male slave and a female slave, and immovable such as real estate if its four boundaries are specified. And this is narrated from Muhammad, and it is upon the later scholars, and it is the one that is given fatwa with due to necessity. In the apparent transmission, it is not accepted for immovable but accepted for movable due to the need for reference to them at time of claim and testimony, unlike real estate and other rights. And from Abu Yusuf that he accepts it for male slaves but not for female slaves due to the prevalence of running away among them rather than female slaves. Then the letter to the judge is of two types: one is the sijill, and the second is called the kitab hukmi as he explained with his statement: 'then if they testify' etc.
'Other than hadd': what is meant by other than hadd and qisas are the rights that are established with doubts and both are averted by doubts. 'Against a present defendant after the plaintiff's claim and the defendant's denial.' 'By the testimony': meaning the binding of the testified matter upon the defendant in favor of the plaintiff.
And he wrote regarding his judgment, and it is called a sijill, otherwise he does not judge. And he wrote the testimony so that the judge, the addressee, may judge by it, and it is the kitab hukmi, and in reality it is the transmission of testimony. The testimony, i.e. the kitab hukmi, is called a sijill by the judge because he recorded it. And he wrote regarding his judgment: indeed the sijill is written so that the event is not forgotten over time and so that the letter is a reminder of it, otherwise there is no need to write the judgment because it was completed in the presence of the defendant himself or his representative, except if he left after the judgment against him or denied the judgment, then at that time he writes to collect the right from him or to execute his judgment. And his statement: 'and it is called a sijill' – the context of this statement may imply that the term sijill is restricted to a writing that established its judgment by the testimony of witnesses, but if the judgment was established by confession and he wrote the judgment, that is also a sijill. So the meaning is that the document that contains the judge's judgment is called a sijill in their custom. 'Sijill': meaning that he made it firm by the judgment, so the sijill only occurs after the judgment. 'Otherwise': meaning if the defendant, i.e. the one sued, is not present. 'He does not judge': meaning the writing judge does not judge by the testimony because judging the absent is not permissible. 'Al-hukmi': it is attributed to hukm (judgment) with consideration of the outcome, and it is not a sijill. 'Transmission of testimony': meaning the kitab hukmi has the transmission of testimony, and the difference between it and the sijill is that the sijill only occurs after the judgment, while the kitab hukmi only occurs before the judgment. And the judgment of the judge in the sijill, if it occurs in a matter of disagreement, the addressee judge does not have the authority to reject it; rather, he must execute it because the judgment is connected to him, unlike the kitab hukmi, for it is permissible for the addressee to contradict the opinion of the writer and overturn his judgment. And he mentioned the manner of the kitab hukmi: that he writes thus: 'From the judge of Bukhara to the judge of Samarkand: that so-and-so and so-and-so testified before me that the slave named Mubarak, whose description is such-and-such, and his age and value, and his owner is so-and-so, and he came into the possession in Samarkand of so-and-so...' to the end of the letter, and he seals it. When it reaches the judge of... (some unclear text)... the defendant with the slave, and he opens the letter with its conditions mentioned in the text. If the description is not as written, he leaves it. If it is, then if the defendant goes to Bukhara, then that; otherwise he surrenders the slave to the plaintiff, not by way of judgment, and takes the slave himself, and puts a lead seal around his neck and stamps it so that no one accosts him on the road saying he stole it, and he writes to the judge of Bukhara a reply to his letter that he sent the slave's judgment to him. When the letter reaches him, he brings the witnesses who testified in the absence of the slave to testify in his presence, and they point out that he is the property of the plaintiff. But he does not judge; rather, he himself writes to the judge of Samarkand that the witnesses testified in his presence, and he sent him with the slave to him, so that the judge in Samarkand judges against the defendant, and the guarantor is freed from his guarantee. Then it is stipulated that the letter be from a known judge to a known judge, regarding a known matter, for a known plaintiff, against a known defendant. And the identification of these persons is by mentioning their names and lineage to their father and grandfather or tribe. If he does not mention the father's name nor the grandfather, identification is not achieved unless he is well-known by his personal name.
In reality, because the writing judge did not judge by the testimony but rather transmitted it to the addressee to judge by it.
His guarantee, then
Source pages p. 415

Commentary
This passage is from the chapter on the judge's letter to another judge (Kitab al-Qadi ila al-Qadi). It begins by stating the basic ruling: a judge may write to another judge regarding cases other than hadd punishments and qisas (retaliation). The writing judge must be a properly appointed judge by the Imam, capable of leading Friday prayer. The letter is not accepted from an arbitrator. The text then discusses the wisdom of placing this chapter after imprisonment, noting that imprisonment requires one judge whereas a letter requires two. There is a dispute: in the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya), a letter is not accepted if the distance between judges is less than travel distance (approximately three days journey). However, Abu Yusuf holds that if the distance is such that the person cannot go to the judge and return home in one day, it is accepted, and this is the relied-upon position. The passage then addresses the objection that analogy would reject the letter because the judge would not even accept oral testimony from the same person, and there is risk of forgery. But it is permitted due to necessity, supported by the narration that Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) permitted it. This is a consensus except for a narration from Malik who allows it even in hudud and qisas. The Hanafi position excludes hudud and qisas because they are averted by doubts (shubuhat). The types of claims for which the letter is written include debts, marriage, divorce, pre-emption, etc. There is a disagreement within the school regarding non-movable property: in the apparent narration it is not accepted, but the later scholars (mutakhkhirun) accept it due to necessity, and this is the mufta bihi. Abu Yusuf restricts it to male slaves only. The passage then distinguishes between two types of letters: the sijill (record of judgment after judgment) and the kitab hukmi (transmission of testimony before judgment). The sijill is written to preserve the memory of a judgment that has already been pronounced; it is binding on the addressee judge. The kitab hukmi is written before judgment and involves transmitting testimony; the addressee judge is not bound to follow the opinion of the writing judge and may adjudicate independently. The passage provides a detailed example of a kitab hukmi regarding a runaway slave, describing the procedure for sending the slave and witnesses. Finally, it mentions the conditions for the validity of the letter: it must be from a known judge to a known judge, concerning a known matter, with known parties, and full identification by name and lineage. The overall thrust is to establish the permissibility and procedure of judicial correspondence by necessity while safeguarding against forgery and maintaining proper judicial authority.

Key Terms
كتاب القاضي (kitab al-qadi): A written communication from one judge to another regarding a legal case, either informing of a judgment (sijill) or transmitting testimony (kitab hukmi).
سجل (sijill): A written document recording a judgment that has already been pronounced. It serves as a record so that the judgment is not forgotten. It is issued after the judge has passed judgment.
كتاب حكمي (kitab hukmi): A letter from a judge forwarding testimony of witnesses to another judge, before any judgment is made. The addressee judge then adjudicates based on that testimony. It is essentially a transfer of evidence.
حد (hadd): Fixed punishments prescribed by Islamic law for specific crimes (e.g., theft, fornication). In this context, a case involving hadd is excepted from the judge's letter due to shubha.
قود (qisas): Retaliation, specifically in cases of murder or bodily harm. Like hudud, it is excepted from the judge's letter because it is averted by doubts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why is a judge's letter not accepted in cases involving hadd (fixed punishments) or qisas (retaliation)?
A) Because the letter is not considered strong evidence.
B) Because hudud and qisas are averted by doubts (shubuhat), and the letter carries a suspicion of forgery.
C) Because the writing judge is not qualified to write such a letter.
D) Because the addressee judge has no authority to execute hadd punishments.

Key Takeaway
The judge's letter is a necessity-based exception to qiyas, accepted for most cases except hudud and qisas, and the mufta bihi position even includes immovable property due to necessity.
